## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration with state variables x (position) and v (velocity), matching second-order ODE models of (non)linear harmonic oscillators. Common structures decompose acceleration into restoring forces f(x), damping g(v,x), and optional time-dependent forcing h(t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Undamped linear oscillator (Hooke/Newton form): dv_dt = -c0 * x (ideal mass-spring restoring acceleration)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (small-amplitude oscillator with linear drag)
- Duffing (hardening/softening spring): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (cubic stiffness nonlinearity plus damping)
- General polynomial restoring force: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) - c3 * v (approximation of nonlinear potential near equilibrium)
- Nonlinear (amplitude-dependent) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (e.g., quadratic/cubic drag effects)
- Quadratic velocity drag (directional): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like drag in 1D motion)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - x**2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited oscillator / limit cycle via negative damping at small |x|)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-based self-excitation): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - v**2) * v - c2 * x (limit cycle via nonlinear damping in v)
- Pendulum-like restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (large-angle oscillator with viscous damping)
- Driven nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness / Mathieu-type behavior)
- Dry friction / stick-slip surrogate: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * tanh(c3 * v) (Coulomb friction approximated smoothly near v=0)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force → dv_dt dominated by a function of x only (often odd in x), indicating an underlying potential V(x) with dv_dt ≈ -dV/dx.
- Linear damping → term proportional to v with negative sign; produces exponential decay of oscillation amplitude in time.
- Hardening/softening stiffness → cubic term in x (x**3) changes frequency with amplitude; sign controls hardening (positive) vs softening (negative).
- Self-excited limit cycles → state-dependent damping such as (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v yields negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude.
- Quadratic drag → v*Abs(v) term indicates direction-dependent dissipative force typical of higher-Re flows or large-speed motion.
- Geometric nonlinearity (pendulum) → sin(c*x) restoring term implies bounded force and amplitude-dependent period without polynomial blow-up.
- External driving → additive periodic term in t (sin/cos of c*t) leads to resonance, beating, and potential chaotic response when combined with nonlinear stiffness.
- Parametric resonance → time-multiplying stiffness term like (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x can destabilize the trivial equilibrium even without direct forcing.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO39)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*exp(-Abs(x))*v - mu*(c1 - v**c2)*v
Candidate formulas: 82

GT (fully expanded):
\[
F(x,t,v)=0.3852302349\sin t\;-\;0.1114436972\,v\,e^{-|x|}\;-\;0.3325884184\,v(1-v^2)\;-\;0.05896131021\,v^3.
\]
Expand the polynomial-in-\(v\) part:
\[
-0.3325884184\,v(1-v^2)= -0.3325884184\,v +0.3325884184\,v^3.
\]
So
\[
F=0.3852302349\sin t\;-\;0.3325884184\,v\;+\;(0.3325884184-0.05896131021)\,v^3\;-\;0.1114436972\,v\,e^{-|x|}.
\]
Thus GT is exactly a sum of four independent basis terms:
- \(\sin t\)
- \(v\)
- \(v^3\)
- \(v e^{-|x|}\)

with **no** constant offset, no \(x\) term, no \(t\) term, no \(x\)-polynomial term, etc. Crucially, the \(x\)-dependence is \(e^{-|x|}\), which is **not** representable as \(e^{k x}\) for all real \(x\) (because \(|x|\) is piecewise: \(e^{-|x|}=e^{-x}\) for \(x\ge0\) and \(e^{x}\) for \(x<0\)).

Below, each candidate is checked for whether its free constants can make it exactly these four terms globally (for all real \(x,t,v\)), respecting the strict rule that \(|x|\) cannot be dropped.

---

### 1. \(c0 v + c1\sin(c2+c3 t)+ c4\sin(c5 t+c6)+ c7 v^3 + c8 v e^{c9 x}\)
Can match \(\sin t\) using one sine term (set the other sine amplitude to 0). Can match \(v\) and \(v^3\). But the exponential term is \(v e^{c9 x}\), not \(v e^{-|x|}\). No choice of constant \(c9\) makes \(e^{c9 x}=e^{-|x|}\) for all real \(x\). **No match**.

### 2. Similar to (1) but with cosine term
Cosine can be phase-shifted to sine, so time part is fine. Still only has \(v e^{c6 x}\), not \(v e^{-|x|}\). **No match**.

### 3. Has \(c7 x\cos(c8 t)\)
GT has no \(x\cos(\cdot)\) term; must set \(c7=0\). Then same issue: \(v e^{c6 x}\neq v e^{-|x|}\). **No match**.

### 4–5. Include \(e^{c5 t}\)
GT has no \(e^{(\cdot)t}\); must set that coefficient 0. Still left with \(v e^{c8 x}\) not \(e^{-|x|}\). **No match** for both.

### 6. Has \(v\sin(\cdot)\)
GT has no \(v\)-modulated sinusoid; must set that coefficient 0. Still wrong \(x\)-dependence in exponential. **No match**.

### 7–12. Include power-in-\(t\) or linear \(t\) or constants
GT has no standalone \(t\) terms or constant offsets; those coefficients must be 0. After removing them, still only \(v e^{k x}\). **No match** for 7–12.

### 13. Extra \(e^{c8 x}\log(c9|v|+1)\)
GT has no \(\log\) term; must set its coefficient 0. Remaining exponential is \(e^{c6 x}\), not \(e^{-|x|}\). **No match**.

### 14–15. Include \(\log(c5 v+1)\)
GT has no \(\log\) in \(v\); must set that coefficient 0. Still wrong exponential in \(x\). **No match**.

### 16–17. Extra \(e^{c8 v}\cos(c9 x)\) or \(\log(\cdot e^{c9 v}+1)\)
GT has no such nonlinear \(v\) terms; must set coefficients 0. Still wrong \(e^{c6 x}\). **No match**.

### 18–19. Include \(v^{c5}\)
GT only needs \(v\) and \(v^3\); could set that term off (coefficient 0) or set exponent to 1 or 3, but still need \(v e^{-|x|}\) and only have \(v e^{c8 x}\). **No match**.

### 22. Has \(\log(c6 x+1)\) and cosine

### 26. Contains \(v e^{c9|x|}\) (this is promising form-wise)
Candidate: \(c0 x + c1 v + c2\sin(c3 t+c4)+ c5 e^{c6 x}+ c7 v^3 + c8 v e^{c9|x|}\).
We can set \(c0=0\) (no \(x\) term), \(c5=0\) (no pure \(e^{c6 x}\)), choose sine to match \(0.38523\sin t\), choose \(c1\) and \(c7\) to match the \(v\) and \(v^3\) coefficients.
Key issue: GT needs \(-0.11144\, v e^{-|x|}\). Candidate has \(c8 v e^{c9|x|}\). We can set \(c9=-1\) and \(c8=-0.1114436972\), giving exactly \(v e^{-|x|}\). This matches the absolute value dependence correctly and globally.
So (26) **can** match GT exactly.
